<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_74f7aeba-a47e-4d2b-b8e4-1eff8018c813'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="review_1758728518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1758728518" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1758728518?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545941082" href="/book/show/28855782-frozen-charlotte">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1758728518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15885547597947292771"><b>3.5 stars.</b><br/><br/>Creepy. Creepy. Creepy. Creepy. <br/><br/>There may exist thousands of books featuring creepy, Machiavellian talking dolls, but they’re a classic that will forever invade horror stories. <br/><br/>To my surprise, I wasn’t scared by this book. Maybe you’ve noticed, it’s shelved under the ‘‘horror’’ genre, which is a genre that I absolutely do not read. Ever. Even if you beg me to.<br/><br/>But this didn’t scare me in the teensiest bit. I was, however, captivated by the story and, of course, creeped out by the dead d</span>
  <span id="freeText15885547597947292771" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars.</b><br /><br />Creepy. Creepy. Creepy. Creepy. <br /><br />There may exist thousands of books featuring creepy, Machiavellian talking dolls, but they’re a classic that will forever invade horror stories. <br /><br />To my surprise, I wasn’t scared by this book. Maybe you’ve noticed, it’s shelved under the ‘‘horror’’ genre, which is a genre that I absolutely do not read. Ever. Even if you beg me to.<br /><br />But this didn’t scare me in the teensiest bit. I was, however, captivated by the story and, of course, creeped out by the dead dolls. <br /><br />The story is well-told. Alex Bell keeps things interesting by adding constant action and twists at unexpected places. Plus I can’t complain about the writing.<br /><br />There really was no need for an unrequited love tragedy, however. Bleh. The story would also have worked even without the imminent romance. It’s really not a main focus, so there’s that, but it could certainly have staid completely dead, too. Pun oh so intended.<br /><br />A bit clichéd, as we’ve all probably seen dozens of movies with cruel dolls or read books about them, so there isn’t a great amount of originality from the author’s part, but I can assure you that it’s very much readable. <br /><br />So much that I’m disappointed this won’t be released for Halloween. What were they thinking releasing this a month from Christmas? Ah, Publishing, a mysterious creature.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15885547597947292771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1124359936" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124359936" />
    <a title="Kimberly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17371689-kimberly"><img alt="Kimberly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404147069p2/17371689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1124359936?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kimberly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kimberly" href="/user/show/17371689-kimberly">Kimberly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17371689-kimberly?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124359936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14868982031491550398">The atmosphere and characterization really drew me into this story. Once I started it (with a suitably creepy prologue that immediately reeled me in), I read the entire book straight through! The main characters are primarily teenaged kids, and one younger. I've read other reviews saying this was a young adult novel, but I found the premise (and those horrible dolls!) to be something that captured my attention and gave me genuine chills in several scenes. The descriptions were at times, very viv</span>
  <span id="freeText14868982031491550398" style="display:none">The atmosphere and characterization really drew me into this story. Once I started it (with a suitably creepy prologue that immediately reeled me in), I read the entire book straight through! The main characters are primarily teenaged kids, and one younger. I've read other reviews saying this was a young adult novel, but I found the premise (and those horrible dolls!) to be something that captured my attention and gave me genuine chills in several scenes. The descriptions were at times, very vivid, and I could almost "hear" the scratching of minuscule fingertips on a glass cabinet, desperate to be unleashed.<br /><br />The backstory and tragedies associated with this house were riveting, and filled with enough details to really get your imagination going in overdrive. In fact, my only minor "complaint" would be that I would have liked to have learned more about the origin of the Frozen Charlotte dolls, and how/why they were introduced in the first place. Although some parts of the story will be predictable to seasoned horror readers, the characterization and added mystery really make up for that, and I never once felt like "skimming" through any of the details.<br /><br />This was my first story by Alex Bell, and I am looking forward to reading more from her in the future. A good, unsettling book, perfect for late night reading.... :)<br /><br />Recommended!<br /><br />*I received a copy of this book from NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.*</span>
  <a data-text-id="14868982031491550398" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1612729895?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=horror-hazes">horror-hazes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1612729895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16156506756846007292">So the line of creepy dolls adorning this book's front cover should have clued me in to the fact that, upon reading this, I would be unable to have an easy night of sleep for quite some time! I read 'YA horror' and assumed this to be a tame, but thrilling story. Oh boy, how wrong could I be!?<br/><br/>Sophie anticipated her stay with her cousin to provide a few weeks of freedom and fun. However, haunted by the tragic death of her best friend and the spooky circumstances that led up to his demise, she arri</span>
  <span id="freeText16156506756846007292" style="display:none">So the line of creepy dolls adorning this book's front cover should have clued me in to the fact that, upon reading this, I would be unable to have an easy night of sleep for quite some time! I read 'YA horror' and assumed this to be a tame, but thrilling story. Oh boy, how wrong could I be!?<br /><br />Sophie anticipated her stay with her cousin to provide a few weeks of freedom and fun. However, haunted by the tragic death of her best friend and the spooky circumstances that led up to his demise, she arrives bringing more baggage than just her psychical ones. Her cousins, already consumed by their own grief, have no room to support any more. Since the death of their sibling Rebecca, years before, the family has forever been fractured, and Sophie had no idea how deep the fissures run. Now the smiling cousins she remembers from her youth are sombre and burdened individuals. And Sophie is left to repair both the memory of this once-happy family as well as discerning the particulars of her best friend's death, alone. But maybe she isn't as alone as she first thought...<br /><br />I was overwhelmed with how aggressive the shock factor of this book was! Instead of an introduction to the characters and an overview of their lives, before sh*t got cray, the reader is invited to a seance, views a ghostly visitation, and oversees a death all within the first few pages! From this pulse-quickening beginning the story does not let up any of its pace until the final page if turned.<br /><br />Once Sophie is reunited with her family I assumed the chill I felt whilst reading this would abate. If the protagonist is to be continually surrounded by other individuals then surely this high-stakes horror could not continue? And this is where I found that the setting would continue to play as big a part in the tense dread, that pervades every aspect of this book, as the plot line.<br /><br />Sophie's cousin reside in the converted Dunvegan School for Girls, on the rural and dreary Isle of Skye. The setting alone is enough to infuse each scene with a pervading sense of eeriness. In much the same way of traditional Gothic texts, that I so adore, the 'haunted mansion' setting fills this book with shadowed corners and creaking stairs that both heighten the actual horrors contained there and provide additional fears, real and imaged, for the reader to obsess over.<br /><br />The events that occur are supernatural and sinister from the outset and continue in much the same vein, only more pronounced, once removed to this isolated setting. The brutality of the scenes and the haunting creep of dread that infuse every single chapter make this a macabre dream for any horror fan. For that reason, this makes this not a book suited to a younger audience, as I had previously perceived. <br /><br />It was surprisingly heartening to see the horror genre portrayed so brilliantly and vividly in such a contemporary setting and with such a young cast of characters. Both are things I have previously found counter-productive to the chilling atmosphere the genre is meant to provide the reader with. I have found that modern technology often ruins much of the suspension of belief that the reader contributes to a historical horror, and a younger character set can often be synonymous with tame horror. Both of these assumptions were eradicated within the first few chapters of this book and Bell did not allow the suspense or eeriness to slip even one iota as the novel progressed. Equal parts chilling as thrilling, this horror is sugar and spice, and none of its nice!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16156506756846007292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3338428421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1726132406836202717">"Now Charlotte lives on the ,mountainside ,<br/>In a bleak and dreary spot.<br/>There was no house for miles around,<br/>except her father's cot."<br/><br/>Frozen Charlotte (Frozen Charlotte, #1)<br/>by Alex Bell<br/><br/>My review:<br/><br/>Do NOT expect to clear your head of this book quickly if you choose to read this.<br/><br/>Finally..a book full of scares and crepiness and no gore..well..very little anyway.<br/><br/><br/>You know what? I am not even going to do a plot summary..don't look. Go in, knowing little.<br/><br/>This is a horror novel about dolls. And about twisted</span>
  <span id="freeText1726132406836202717" style="display:none">"Now Charlotte lives on the ,mountainside ,<br />In a bleak and dreary spot.<br />There was no house for miles around,<br />except her father's cot."<br /><br />Frozen Charlotte (Frozen Charlotte, #1)<br />by Alex Bell<br /><br />My review:<br /><br />Do NOT expect to clear your head of this book quickly if you choose to read this.<br /><br />Finally..a book full of scares and crepiness and no gore..well..very little anyway.<br /><br /><br />You know what? I am not even going to do a plot summary..don't look. Go in, knowing little.<br /><br />This is a horror novel about dolls. And about twisted happenings and things that go bump in the night.<br /><br />Recommended to read at night..after it gets dark.<br /><br />It isn't that this is the scariest book I have ever read. It is just the EERIE factor..wow. Somehow this creepy little book manages to remain creepy and eerie through the whole thing. No easy feat.<br /><br />Elements are disturbing and I really think Stephen King would love this.<br /><br />Images conjured up do not leave one's head anytime soon.<br /><br />There are a few parts that are a little funny..like why the HECK did Sophie not leave in the first HOUR? OK..she wanted to find out how her friend died..but listen this poor chick has more happen to her in 24 hours than most do in a lifetime. She deserves the medal of honor for not leaving.<br /><br />In spite of how creepy this book was it isn't a five star read. And now I will say that if you plan to read this:<br /><br />Stop reading my review.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />No explanation is ever given for what happened to Jay. We KNOW..or think we do..that it wasn't Rebecca. But Piper wasn't dead. So it would not be her either. So..who? Why was Jay killed? And by whom? No explanation is ever given and I almost rated it a 3 because of that since it was a major plot hole. I really wish someone could fill in the blanks.<br /><br />No matter. It was quite a freaky read and what I did not mention? The Charlotte back story, in which each chapter begins with a short limerick like the one I posted above, is interestingly just as creepy as the other aspects of the book. We get the story from one of the characters in the book but it is made more eerie by the quotes at the story of each chapter which are spooky enough to give one a chill..that was incredibly done.<br /><br /> <br />This was a real scare fest and thanks Meisha for the recommendation.</span>

<div id="review_2265137986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265137986" />
    <a title="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond"><img alt="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494279381p2/47129377.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2265137986?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie (TBR and Beyond)" href="/user/show/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond">Melanie (TBR and Beyond)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780545941082" href="/book/show/28855782-frozen-charlotte">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=ya-paranormal">ya-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=ya-horror">ya-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=no-romance">no-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=siblings">siblings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47129377-melanie-tbr-and-beyond?shelf=top-2018-reads">top-2018-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2265137986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13171071353294652235"><br/><b>Trigger Warning: Graphic violence that involve children, self harm and creepy ass little dolls. </b><br/><br/><br/>Wow! What a dark little YA horror gem I found in this book. This one is not for the faint of heart. <br/><br/>I have no idea where to even begin with this review. What a strange, dark story. I actually picked this up at the library because I saw the cover and thought it might be a cute, fast read. There is basically NOTHING about this book where the word "cute" would describe it. The YA horror genre is pretty l</span>
  <span id="freeText13171071353294652235" style="display:none"><br /><b>Trigger Warning: Graphic violence that involve children, self harm and creepy ass little dolls. </b><br /><br /><br />Wow! What a dark little YA horror gem I found in this book. This one is not for the faint of heart. <br /><br />I have no idea where to even begin with this review. What a strange, dark story. I actually picked this up at the library because I saw the cover and thought it might be a cute, fast read. There is basically NOTHING about this book where the word "cute" would describe it. The YA horror genre is pretty lacking and usually does not offer anything very unnerving or interesting. I thought this book was both. <br /><br />Our main protagonist, Sophie, has to go stay with relatives when her friend unexpectedly dies after a rather bizarre encounter using an Ouija board app on their phone. The encounter leads Sophie wanting more answers and she thinks she may be able to get them by staying with her uncle, whose daughter Charlotte had died years before. This book starts off dark and stays dark. The second the MC gets to her uncle's home, she is greeted by some by his very strange children. The oldest daughter is basically a stepford-wife, the brother's hand was melted in a fire and goes around having fits and then you have the littlest one who is afraid of bones. Being afraid of bones might not seem like something all the creepy but you'd be dead wrong. The author went as far as having the five year old scared so badly off bones that she wants her own skeleton out of her body so they have to hide the knives so she won't try and cut them out. I mean when I say dark, I mean DARKKKK. My mouth dropped a few times, since this was YA and the style of writing almost read like an older middle-grade. I would've marked it as middle-grade if some of the topics weren't so graphic. <br /><br />I don't really want to say too much about this one because going in as blind as possible is the best thing. I watch tons of horror films so this book didn't scare me but I did still find it disturbing. I think your average non-horror reader would find this one really creepy though and it does have the potential for nightmares. I loved that the dolls ended up being so tiny - it really just added to the atmosphere the author had created. <br /><br />I'm torn on whether I would recommend this book, since the subject matter could possibly offend or bother some. I guess if you don't mind books dealing with what I discussed in this review than I'd go check this one out. It's great if you're a horror/paranormal fan. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13171071353294652235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1622513638" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1622513638" />
    <a title="Shaikha Alahmad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55334362-shaikha-alahmad"><img alt="Shaikha Alahmad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583758717p2/55334362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1622513638?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaikha Alahmad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaikha Alahmad" href="/user/show/55334362-shaikha-alahmad">Shaikha Alahmad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1622513638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3104656430627848398"><i>THIS IS HIGHLY RECOMMENDED FOR HORROR/GHOSTS/WALKING-TALKING DOLLS FANS!</i><br/><br/><br/>OH MY GOD, I <b>LOVE</b> THIS!<br/><br/>Stumbling upon this book and buying it is the BEST decision I've made, it seriously scared the shit out of me! FANTASTIC horror writing, the twists and turns, everything is absolute PERFECTION! There were times when I couldn't even read this alone. I'm 100% sure that this book will stick with me throughout my life since it gave me lots of nightmares recently (& I don't even mean this in a bad way, it's</span>
  <span id="freeText3104656430627848398" style="display:none"><i>THIS IS HIGHLY RECOMMENDED FOR HORROR/GHOSTS/WALKING-TALKING DOLLS FANS!</i><br /><br /><br />OH MY GOD, I <b>LOVE</b> THIS!<br /><br />Stumbling upon this book and buying it is the BEST decision I've made, it seriously scared the shit out of me! FANTASTIC horror writing, the twists and turns, everything is absolute PERFECTION! There were times when I couldn't even read this alone. I'm 100% sure that this book will stick with me throughout my life since it gave me lots of nightmares recently (&amp; I don't even mean this in a bad way, it's just how awesome this book is).<br /><br />Now "Frozen Charlotte Dolls" is all what I google about, it turns out you can find a lot of creepy stories and articles about these dolls, no joke, I found it super interesting. I really want to know the story of how the dolls got haunted in the first place (or at least how people thought they were) since the book doesn't provide this information.<br /><br />Thank you Alex Bell for creating this masterpiece! ❤</span>

<div id="review_2159807374" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159807374" />
    <a title="murphy ✌ (daydreamofalife)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36233173-murphy-daydreamofalife"><img alt="murphy ✌ (daydreamofalife)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590900648p2/36233173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159807374?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="murphy ✌ (daydreamofalife)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="murphy ✌ (daydreamofalife)" href="/user/show/36233173-murphy-daydreamofalife">murphy ✌ (daydreamofalife)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23899301-frozen-charlotte">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36233173-murphy-daydreamofalife?shelf=read-as-ebook">read-as-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36233173-murphy-daydreamofalife?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36233173-murphy-daydreamofalife?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159807374" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11783066842210629895">1.5 / 5<br/><br/>Decently spooky with ouija, death, a creepy house, and evil dolls.<br/><br/>I think if I'd read this before the age of like, fifteen or so, it would've been a 5-star read, as my taste and expectations weren't quite as developed then as they are now. I tend to lean towards longer and more character driven works, and this didn't really fit the bill.<br/><br/>The characters fell quite flat for me. Our leading lady Sophie was probably the most well-developed, but I can't say that I ever really liked her. Her unc</span>
  <span id="freeText11783066842210629895" style="display:none">1.5 / 5<br /><br />Decently spooky with ouija, death, a creepy house, and evil dolls.<br /><br />I think if I'd read this before the age of like, fifteen or so, it would've been a 5-star read, as my taste and expectations weren't quite as developed then as they are now. I tend to lean towards longer and more character driven works, and this didn't really fit the bill.<br /><br />The characters fell quite flat for me. Our leading lady Sophie was probably the most well-developed, but I can't say that I ever really liked her. Her uncle was barely there at all, almost as if he were just an afterthought. And her cousins? They were weird. Cameron was broody and prone to violent outbursts. Piper was almost cookie-cutter perfect for the majority of the book and then <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a sociopath <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> for the rest. And Lilias seemed like she was just there as a plot point, someone to move the story along when it came to a halt. <br /><br />The writing wasn't bad, but it wasn't special either. It was a pretty fast and easy read, so I guess that's a pro? But some of the dialogue was a bit weird, it seemed overly proper and stilted, and every character talked exactly the same. <br /><br />The plot seemed to introduce a lot of strings and forget about them later. I mean, the book starts with Sophie being motivated to find the truth about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her best friend Jay's death and how it connects to her dead cousin Rebecca, who they called on through a ouija phone app <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but I don't really think that it was resolved at all? It seems like the plot got too busy and the initial mystery got left behind in the dirt. What was the connection between <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jay's death <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the rest of the story? Even Sophie eventually forgot that she found it suspicious and just moved on to the mysteries with her cousins and the Frozen Charlotte dolls. And speaking of the damn dolls, yeah I guess they were pretty creepy and awful, but I kind of feel cheated? Are all Frozen Charlotte dolls in the world secretly evil? Is it just the ones in the house (which used to be an old school) and if so, why? Why are these dolls able to inspire bad behavior? I guess I just wanted like an origin story or something, but they were pretty much just there to be an evil plot point.<br /><br />I think the thing that bothered me most was that this book kind of seemed like a plot outline? Almost like it needed more filler, or <i>something</i>, to make sense of getting from point A to point B, because everything seemed so... clear-cut? Uncomplicated? Convenient? I don't know guys. Maybe it was just me? The ratings for this book are pretty up there, so maybe everyone else just got something from this book that I didn't. But overall I'm pretty underwhelmed here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11783066842210629895" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2759175449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9981697050990222813">I'm trying a new thing where I want to start my reviews with buzzwords or buzz phrases about the books. <br/><b>So, buzzwords:<br/>- Creepy dolls<br/>- Creepy houses/mansion that was once an all girl school<br/>- Stormy windy atmosphere<br/>- Mysterious death and injury<br/>- Ghosts</b><br/><br/>There's something about this book that sets it apart from so many other YA horror novels. Generally, YA horror novels are often cliche and silly, rather than creepy and scary. But this book was not at all cliche or silly. I don't get scared or spooke</span>
  <span id="freeText9981697050990222813" style="display:none">I'm trying a new thing where I want to start my reviews with buzzwords or buzz phrases about the books. <br /><b>So, buzzwords:<br />- Creepy dolls<br />- Creepy houses/mansion that was once an all girl school<br />- Stormy windy atmosphere<br />- Mysterious death and injury<br />- Ghosts</b><br /><br />There's something about this book that sets it apart from so many other YA horror novels. Generally, YA horror novels are often cliche and silly, rather than creepy and scary. But this book was not at all cliche or silly. I don't get scared or spooked, but this book definitely was something that had me uneasy throughout. <br /><br />From the first chapter, this book is action packed and creepy. It follows a girl, Sophie, who is in a cafe with her friend one day playing with a Ouiji board app on his phone, when some strange occurrences happen, and they don't stop there. This book just continues to be creepy and atmospheric, and there were several instances when my anxiety kicked in because I was nervous about what was going to happen. <br /><br />I don't really want to say anything more, because I think it's best to go into this with no expectations, but just know mid book I had already ordered the prequel novel because this was <i>that</i> good.</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=creepy">creepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38807240-meisha?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2361633017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14736879930298342530">This was a really fast paced and creepy story. I read a lot of horror and rarely find ones that scare me. And although it didn’t necessarily scare me, there were definitely scenes that REALLY creeped me out and had me glancing over my shoulder. Everything was so vivid and real that I could actually feel the cold air and creepy atmosphere. An added bonus, for those of you that didn’t know, this is not only horror but a mystery novel as well! I found that the mystery aspect really added a lot to t</span>
  <span id="freeText14736879930298342530" style="display:none">This was a really fast paced and creepy story. I read a lot of horror and rarely find ones that scare me. And although it didn’t necessarily scare me, there were definitely scenes that REALLY creeped me out and had me glancing over my shoulder. Everything was so vivid and real that I could actually feel the cold air and creepy atmosphere. An added bonus, for those of you that didn’t know, this is not only horror but a mystery novel as well! I found that the mystery aspect really added a lot to the story and made it more engaging and gripping. It honestly had me on the edge of my seat for a lot of the story. I also found the characters to be likable and three dimensional! The only gripe I had with this book was that the writing was rather juvenile.... But if that’s not something that typically bothers you and you’re able to get past it, I think this a story that a lot of people would really enjoy! 🙂</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8166172294085011598">Summary:<br/><br/>Sophia goes to spend the summer with her uncle and cousins in their former schoolhouse home following the death of her best friend. <br/>Once arriving, she realizes something is very wrong. Her cousin, Rebecca, who died there almost 8 years ago seems to be haunting the house and there is something very disturbing about Rebecca's old collection of frozen charlotte dolls. <br/>As everything begins to fall apart around her, Sophia is left to figure out who or what is causing all the chaos before it's</span>
  <span id="freeText8166172294085011598" style="display:none">Summary:<br /><br />Sophia goes to spend the summer with her uncle and cousins in their former schoolhouse home following the death of her best friend. <br />Once arriving, she realizes something is very wrong. Her cousin, Rebecca, who died there almost 8 years ago seems to be haunting the house and there is something very disturbing about Rebecca's old collection of frozen charlotte dolls. <br />As everything begins to fall apart around her, Sophia is left to figure out who or what is causing all the chaos before it's too late. <br /><br />Personal opinion:<br /><br />This one is a very creepy and sinister page turner that I loved. It had me hooked from right from the beginning with a spooky seance in a crowded cafe. It's not often that a book actually creeps me out, but this one managed to. (Although creepy dolls are one of the few things I don't necessarily like to begin with.)<br />The home's history was a good addition to add even more creepiness and the writing makes it an easy book to binge read, which is exactly what I did with this one. <br />I also have to add that the ending was pretty good as well. I was not expecting it to go the way it did. <br />Even though the main characters are teens and some a bit younger, Frozen Charlotte is definitely more of a YA or adult read. <br />I would definitely recommend to lovers of the weird and creepy!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4579983199259301465">Please note that yes this is a ya book it is not suitable for young ya. Due to the sensitive nature of some of the topics running throughout this book. <br/><br/>I thought this was a pretty good book.   <span id="freeText4579983199259301465" style="display:none">Please note that yes this is a ya book it is not suitable for young ya. Due to the sensitive nature of some of the topics running throughout this book. <br /><br />I thought this was a pretty good book. Very dark covers everything from death, suicide, ouiji boards, evil dolls, demonic spirits, crazy families, secrets, possession, hauntings ect. It's not a read for the faint hearted. <br /><br />It is written really well and is a great introduction into supernatural thrillers. It is quite grown up which is why I also advise that it's not one for young ya or for anyone if a nervous disposition. So choose to let your children read this wisely. <br /><br />But if you think it is for them then I think they will definitely enjoy the edge of your seat. Intriguing and spooky tale. <br /><br />I'm not a massive fan of anything to do with talking/killer dolls so even I found the frozen charlottes a little creepy. The fact that the are real and that they have the rhyme that goes through the chapters of the book is even more creepy. <br /><br />It is written very well and I enjoyed reading it. <br /><br />Happy reading everyone </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13846365824541984907">"Then quickly to the glowing hall, <br/>her lifeless form he bore, <br/>Fair Charlotte's eyes were closed to death, <br/>her voice was heard no more."<br/><br/>I really went into this story thinking 'YA horror, probably going to be a bit tame' but my goodness it really wasn't! It really terrified me to the point I actually had a nightmare about it last night when I had finished reading it.<br/>After a horrific tragedy, Sophie goes to stay with her cousins on the Isle of Skye for 2 weeks while her parents are away in America </span>
  <span id="freeText13846365824541984907" style="display:none">"Then quickly to the glowing hall, <br />her lifeless form he bore, <br />Fair Charlotte's eyes were closed to death, <br />her voice was heard no more."<br /><br />I really went into this story thinking 'YA horror, probably going to be a bit tame' but my goodness it really wasn't! It really terrified me to the point I actually had a nightmare about it last night when I had finished reading it.<br />After a horrific tragedy, Sophie goes to stay with her cousins on the Isle of Skye for 2 weeks while her parents are away in America celebrating their wedding anniversary.<br />Her cousins, Piper, Cameron and Lilias are all very different facets. Piper is welcoming to the point of extreme, Cameron is distant, and Lilias is timid and scared. When Sophie discovers that the house used to be a girl's boarding school, she notices a cabinet full of 'Frozen Charlotte' dolls in one of the bedrooms. These dolls are no bigger than a matchbox, but have hauntingly painted faces and were supposedly invloved in the death of one of the girls at the school... Why is it that Lilias claims they move at night and try to get out of the cabinet? And what was the mystery surrounding Rebecca, the 4th child who died mysteriously on the rocks by the house? And are any of them safe in the house, or from each other?<br />So haunting, this has really stuck with me, and I'll be looking out for the sequel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13846365824541984907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1852696756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1852696756" />
    <a title="Jules" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4824134-jules"><img alt="Jules" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561752629p2/4824134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1852696756?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jules" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jules" href="/user/show/4824134-jules">Jules</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=supernatural">supernatural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4824134-jules?shelf=physical-books-i-own">physical-books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1852696756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4392512414122708111"><i>Frozen Charlotte</i> is a young adult horror. <br/><br/>I’m picky when it comes to choosing YA fiction, and despite being a huge horror fan as a child and teenager, it’s not a genre that I often read these days. The reason I don’t read a lot of YA fiction, is I tend to find they lack the intensity I hope for. But this book was actually surprisingly creepy, tense and rather brutal in places. My teenage self would have loved this book.<br/><br/>I also found the characters interesting, and really felt for them and their s</span>
  <span id="freeText4392512414122708111" style="display:none"><i>Frozen Charlotte</i> is a young adult horror. <br /><br />I’m picky when it comes to choosing YA fiction, and despite being a huge horror fan as a child and teenager, it’s not a genre that I often read these days. The reason I don’t read a lot of YA fiction, is I tend to find they lack the intensity I hope for. But this book was actually surprisingly creepy, tense and rather brutal in places. My teenage self would have loved this book.<br /><br />I also found the characters interesting, and really felt for them and their situation. At times I felt a little trapped and claustrophobic. I was also surprisingly spooked each night when I turned the light off in an attempt to go to sleep. I really need to avoid reading about creepy dolls just before bed!<br /><br />This is definitely one I recommend for those into YA and horror stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4392512414122708111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784226567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14947337410239820510">This had the potential to be truly creepy, but it just threw everything out there, which didn't allow for any suspense to build. There's also a lot of inconsistency in the character of Rebecca, who is by turns evil and menacing or scared and sweet and helpful. In fact, all of the characters have personalities that change when it's convenient to the plot for them to do so. There is no subtlety to this novel at all—it just throws everything on the page which, for me, doesn't work in a ghost story </span>
  <span id="freeText14947337410239820510" style="display:none">This had the potential to be truly creepy, but it just threw everything out there, which didn't allow for any suspense to build. There's also a lot of inconsistency in the character of Rebecca, who is by turns evil and menacing or scared and sweet and helpful. In fact, all of the characters have personalities that change when it's convenient to the plot for them to do so. There is no subtlety to this novel at all—it just throws everything on the page which, for me, doesn't work in a ghost story with creepy dolls. I want subtlety and menace and building dread and didn't find it here.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1148312807" />
    <a title="Hannah (Ivyclad Ideas)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas"><img alt="Hannah (Ivyclad Ideas)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495303756p2/37152129.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1148312807?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah (Ivyclad Ideas)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah (Ivyclad Ideas)" href="/user/show/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas">Hannah (Ivyclad Ideas)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37152129-hannah-ivyclad-ideas?shelf=read-in-a-day">read-in-a-day</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1148312807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12169171062684548758">Motivated by a giant spoiler, Sophie heads off to the Isle of Skye to stay with the cousins she hasn't seen since she was young. Cameron is broody. Piper is perfect. Lilias is strange. And Rebecca? Rebecca is dead. <br/><br/>She was the spirit Sophie chose to summon.<br/><br/>The plot is driven less by Sophie's desire to find out whether the supernatural was responsible for said giant spoiler, and more by Cameron and Piper's constant attempts to paint one another as the villain of the piece. This isn't Sophie's fau</span>
  <span id="freeText12169171062684548758" style="display:none">Motivated by a giant spoiler, Sophie heads off to the Isle of Skye to stay with the cousins she hasn't seen since she was young. Cameron is broody. Piper is perfect. Lilias is strange. And Rebecca? Rebecca is dead. <br /><br />She was the spirit Sophie chose to summon.<br /><br />The plot is driven less by Sophie's desire to find out whether the supernatural was responsible for said giant spoiler, and more by Cameron and Piper's constant attempts to paint one another as the villain of the piece. This isn't Sophie's fault - she's entirely reliant on what her cousins will and won't tell her. What they will tell her is patchy and unreliable. What they won't tell her could fill several books. The suspense builds and builds right up until the climax and is maintained right until the end. I'll admit, I'm bad with suspense, or any sort of mystery. If I don't plough through the entire novel in one go, chances are that I'll pick it up when I'm bored and sleepy and flick right to the end. Disaster averted with this one. Frozen Charlotte held my attention from start to finish.<br /><br />I love a good Gothic horror, and I would definitely class this novel as Gothic. The setting was almost another character, obstructive and antagonistic, it attacked half of the characters and warped the others. Sophie's cousins live on the Isle of Skye, which is only accessible from the British mainland by ferry. This adds to the sense of isolation in the story.<br /><br />A good ghost story is one of my favourite things, and this one doesn't disappoint. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12169171062684548758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1215057849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1215057849" />
    <a title="Ellen Gail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27123577-ellen-gail"><img alt="Ellen Gail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595798462p2/27123577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen Gail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen Gail" href="/user/show/27123577-ellen-gail">Ellen Gail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23899301-frozen-charlotte">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27123577-ellen-gail?shelf=freebie">freebie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27123577-ellen-gail?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27123577-ellen-gail?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1215057849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18329881407658057801"><b>
  <i>"But, miss...they like being dead. They told us."</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412396866i/11370368.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Creepy dolls! Dolls don't majorly freak me out like snakes and other peoples' feet. The exception being ventriloquist dummies, ventriloquist dummies are freaky.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447385675ra/16998905.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Anyway, point is <i>Frozen Charlotte</i> really brings the creeps with the tiniest of dolls. It has a Ouija board (app), a ghost, evil dolls that want you to come be bad with them, and people that are <i>not</i> to be trusted. Despite all of this going on, it's well balanced. There's some great stuff</span>
  <span id="freeText18329881407658057801" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"But, miss...they like being dead. They told us."</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412396866i/11370368.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Creepy dolls! Dolls don't majorly freak me out like snakes and other peoples' feet. The exception being ventriloquist dummies, ventriloquist dummies are freaky.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447385675ra/16998905.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, point is <i>Frozen Charlotte</i> really brings the creeps with the tiniest of dolls. It has a Ouija board (app), a ghost, evil dolls that want you to come be bad with them, and people that are <i>not</i> to be trusted. Despite all of this going on, it's well balanced. There's some great stuff with family and trust going on. Yes, these people are technically Sophie's family, but does she really know any of them that well? Who can she trust? Why should they trust her?<br><br>Then there's the dolls. The Frozen Charlottes don't just want to stab your eyes out with needles, although that would be fun. They want to get into your head and make you think bad things. Do bad things. Eventually, you'll see how fun those games are. They remind me of malicious little porcelain fairies.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Don't you want to play with us any more? It's fun to be dead."</i>
</b><br><br>Overall, <i>Frozen Charlotte</i> was just enormously fun to read. I had a ball reading it, and that counts for so much in deciding where a book falls for me in grand scheme of things. I trust my gut, and my gut says yes to this!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18329881407658057801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1788966006?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gina" href="/user/show/38790407-gina">Gina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/32905492-frozen-charlotte">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38790407-gina?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788966006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10705604890087937612"><b> ** 4.5 SPINE-CHILLING STARS! **</b><br/><br/><i>"Now Charlotte lived on the mountainside,<br/>In a bleak and dreary spot.<br/>There was no house for miles around,<br/>Except her father's cot."</i><br/><br/>***<br/><br/>WHY EXACTLY IS THIS NOT A MOVIE YET?! <br/>This better become a damned movie or I'm filing a complaint. <br/><br/>I <b>loved</b> this book. I literally devoured it in a day because whenever I picked it up, I couldn't bear to put it down and if I did I kept thinking about it which lead to me picking it straight up again. <br/><br/>This is written SO greatly for a YA </span>
  <span id="freeText10705604890087937612" style="display:none"><b> ** 4.5 SPINE-CHILLING STARS! **</b><br /><br /><i>"Now Charlotte lived on the mountainside,<br />In a bleak and dreary spot.<br />There was no house for miles around,<br />Except her father's cot."</i><br /><br />***<br /><br />WHY EXACTLY IS THIS NOT A MOVIE YET?! <br />This better become a damned movie or I'm filing a complaint. <br /><br />I <b>loved</b> this book. I literally devoured it in a day because whenever I picked it up, I couldn't bear to put it down and if I did I kept thinking about it which lead to me picking it straight up again. <br /><br />This is written SO greatly for a YA thriller, you get sucked in within two seconds notice. <br />It's creepy, well-thought of, fast paced,... whatever you want in a thriller you got it in this one. <br />I'd understand if one would be a bit sceptical when you know it's about talking dolls and involves a Ouija-board but TRUST MEEEEEEEE, it's so much more and put together so smartly. <br /><br />Every so often there was someone else's you'd suspect as the disturbed one until a certain point where you think "okay now I've got it, y'all can't trick me into suspecting anyone else anymore!!!" and then you find out it's someone else anyway. <br />This book keeps you guessing, it keeps you on the edge of your seat and it actually manages to take you there yourself and make you believe everything she writes. <br /><br /><br />It's great and it made me want to pick up another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/942248.Alex_Bell" title="Alex Bell" rel="nofollow noopener">Alex Bell</a> book immediately! Too bad I don't have any. <b>yet.</b><br />I would a 100% recommend this if you're into thrillers or were thinking of trying one out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10705604890087937612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1083864948" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083864948" />
    <a title="Chrissi " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5858987-chrissi"><img alt="Chrissi " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311418743p2/5858987.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083864948?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chrissi " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chrissi " href="/user/show/5858987-chrissi">Chrissi </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083864948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14300821520119998440">I think it’s safe to say that I’m not the biggest fan of horror. My imagination runs away with me and things play on my mind for ages after I’ve read a book. I still have vivid memories of a part of a Chris Wooding book that will forever stay in my memory! However, I was SO intrigued by Frozen Charlotte that I knew I wanted to read it. Even if I had to take breaks between chapters to focus my mind elsewhere… I tore through Frozen Charlotte despite the breaks I took whilst reading it…it was incre</span>
  <span id="freeText14300821520119998440" style="display:none">I think it’s safe to say that I’m not the biggest fan of horror. My imagination runs away with me and things play on my mind for ages after I’ve read a book. I still have vivid memories of a part of a Chris Wooding book that will forever stay in my memory! However, I was SO intrigued by Frozen Charlotte that I knew I wanted to read it. Even if I had to take breaks between chapters to focus my mind elsewhere… I tore through Frozen Charlotte despite the breaks I took whilst reading it…it was incredibly creepy. I’m just glad I don’t have any dolls in the house!<br /><br />Frozen Charlotte follows Sophie and her cousins Cameron, Lilias and Piper as Sophie spends summer with them. The prologue gripped me immediately. It starts with Sophie and her friend Jay mucking around with a Ouija board app which certainly has consequences. I raced through the book as Sophie went to visit her Uncle and cousins in Scotland at the creepy schoolhouse. It was incredibly creepy. I found the setting so atmospheric. It’s definitely a book that I could easily see being adapted for TV or film. It would make a great teenage horror film.<br /><br />At her Uncle’s house, Sophie hears things going bump in the night and she hears voices seeming to be coming from the creepy Frozen Charlotte dolls in her deceased cousin’s bedroom. Sophie is sure there is a link between the dolls and her friend Jay. She’s determined to find out more about the incidents that keep occurring and why her Uncle’s house is plagued with bad luck.<br /><br />Alex Bell’s writing is exciting and easy to read. I found myself wanting to read more as each chapter hooked me a little further. The pace of the book was fantastic and made me devour it! Frozen Charlotte is well worth reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14300821520119998440" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17736369837472532526">I bought this book un-researched, based on title and blurb alone. This doesn't happen very often, I usually check the goodread rating on pretty much any book before buying it. In this particular case though, I had forgotten my phone at home and couldn't.<br/><br/>I started reading the book immediately and was drawn in at once. The book had all the elements of an old-fashioned horror story: ouija board, spirit, evil dolls, old school house, deaths by accidents and untrustworthy friends. Perhaps not brillia</span>
  <span id="freeText17736369837472532526" style="display:none">I bought this book un-researched, based on title and blurb alone. This doesn't happen very often, I usually check the goodread rating on pretty much any book before buying it. In this particular case though, I had forgotten my phone at home and couldn't.<br /><br />I started reading the book immediately and was drawn in at once. The book had all the elements of an old-fashioned horror story: ouija board, spirit, evil dolls, old school house, deaths by accidents and untrustworthy friends. Perhaps not brilliantly original, but definintely delightfully put together. <br /><br />Sophie arrives at her cousins' on the isle of Skye. They live in an old school house that was shut down after a multitude of accidents. One of Sophie's cousins, Rebecca, also died in an accident. Sophie is determined to find out more about why, but her cousins aren't exactly forth-coming. Piper seems friendly enough, but her brother Cameron is a gloomy sort with a ruined hand and equally ruined prospect of a career in music and little sister Lilias seems deeply disturbed. Their mother is in a mental hospital.<br /><br />This is a quick and highly entertaining read that fulfilled all my expectations. Never trust appearances! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17736369837472532526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1804657595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1804657595" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27151715-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513668062p2/27151715.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1804657595?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/27151715-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=horror-thriller-mystery">horror-thriller-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27151715-kelly?shelf=physical-owned">physical-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1804657595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13854145832696531223"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I hate dolls. I have to start by saying this because this book is all about creepy little dolls and it really freaked me out. I’ve never been more grateful that I don’t have a load of dolls in my bedroom or I probably wouldn’t have slept since reading this book.<br/><br/><i>Frozen Charlotte</i> is a book I had heard a lot of people raving about. It is not often that I dip into horror books but the idea of this one just wouldn’t leave me and it had been on my shelf for nearly a year so the Halloween Read</span>
  <span id="freeText13854145832696531223" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I hate dolls. I have to start by saying this because this book is all about creepy little dolls and it really freaked me out. I’ve never been more grateful that I don’t have a load of dolls in my bedroom or I probably wouldn’t have slept since reading this book.<br /><br /><i>Frozen Charlotte</i> is a book I had heard a lot of people raving about. It is not often that I dip into horror books but the idea of this one just wouldn’t leave me and it had been on my shelf for nearly a year so the Halloween Readathon seemed like the perfect time to read it. Needless to say I absolutely loved it and read the whole thing from cover to cover in one sitting (no, not just because I was too scared to move).<br /><br />From the very first few pages this book creeped me out. I loved that the book didn’t shy away from modern day technologies and that when Sophie and Jay did an Ouija board it was through an app on Jay’s phone. Little did they know what they were about to unleash and in some very frightening first opening scenes I knew exactly what I was in for during this book, or at least I thought I did.<br /><br />This book ticked a lot of the typical horror clichés: a mysterious death, a scary house, creepy little girl, weird brother, family secrets and DOLLS. There were a few scenes in the book where I did actually find myself lifting my feet from the floor so that I wouldn’t imagine a freezing cold hand reaching out to my ankle. The horror elements of this book are SO well written and genuinely very creepy. I didn’t realise until after reading the book and doing a Google search that Frozen Charlotte dolls are an actual real thing which definitely creeped me out more!<br /><br />I don’t want to give too much away about the plot but I really loved all of the twists and turns along the way. Every time I thought I knew where the book was going it took another twist and left me stunned. There is a huge climax towards the end of this book that had my heart pounding and I thought the ending was really sweet too. Although that epilogue definitely sent a shiver down my spine!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13854145832696531223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1949011705" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1949011705" />
    <a title="Suad Shamma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma"><img alt="Suad Shamma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507364224p2/11245979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1949011705?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suad Shamma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suad Shamma" href="/user/show/11245979-suad-shamma">Suad Shamma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11245979-suad-shamma?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1949011705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14658332802971912336">This is the perfect time of year to read this book if you're interested in a spine-tingling, bone-chilling, good ol' classic horror tale! Although, if you read it at any other time of year, it will still be just as frighteningly creepy!<br/><br/>I love books that really get to you to the point where you actually end up looking over your shoulder and losing sleep over them. That's how much this book affected me. It's been a long time since I read a good thriller, in which I was truly scared to flip the pag</span>
  <span id="freeText14658332802971912336" style="display:none">This is the perfect time of year to read this book if you're interested in a spine-tingling, bone-chilling, good ol' classic horror tale! Although, if you read it at any other time of year, it will still be just as frighteningly creepy!<br /><br />I love books that really get to you to the point where you actually end up looking over your shoulder and losing sleep over them. That's how much this book affected me. It's been a long time since I read a good thriller, in which I was truly scared to flip the page and read what happens next. When you watch a movie, you have the option of covering your eyes through the scary bits, but what do you do when you're reading a book? That night, I couldn't go to sleep until I had finished it, and I made my husband stay up with me until I did. Except, he didn't - he couldn't. So I read the book while he slept soundly next to me and I held his arm in a death grip. The creepiness levels of the book are super high, which is amazing for this genre, because it's not always easy to achieve the 'shivers-down-your-back' sensation.<br /><br />From the very beginning, when Sophie is sitting with her best friend Jay in a diner and he presents her with an app of a Ouija board, you know things are not going to end well. Nothing ever ends well with a Ouija board! Sophie can't take him seriously, but humors him, and soon after the lights in the diner go off, and while chaos ensues, Sophie could swear she could see a little girl standing on the table. When they lights are back on, Sophie and Jay both brush the whole thing off as a coincidence, and call it a night. Except, the next morning, Sophie is told that Jay had died in an accident on his way home. Her parents had planned on going on a trip and dropping her off to her uncle's house, but upon hearing the news of Jay, they tell her they will cancel and stay with her. Sophie stubbornly refuses, and tells them she needs the space right now, so spending time at her uncle's on the Isle of Skye is perfect. Now, I don't know, if as a parent, seeing my child's grief, I would have gone and left them, regardless of how much I paid for a ticket. However, for the purposes of this story, I let that one slide and just enjoyed it. <br /><br />So Sophie arrives at her uncle's house, which used to be a girls schoolhouse that was shut down after a series of murders had occurred, to spend the summer with her cousins - Cameron, Piper and Lilias. There also used to be a fourth cousin, Rebecca, but she died in an accident and they don't talk about her. <br /><br />Sophie can immediately sense something's off about this entire place, but can't put her finger on it, and assumes this is just her grief and guilt over Jay's death creating all these dark and somber images. She immediately hits it off with Piper, who is always exuding charm and positivity as she takes over as host and prepares the food and shows her around. Cameron, on the other hand, is more of a recluse and not particularly friendly either, self-conscious about his scarred hand and bitter about the fact that he can't play the piano anymore. For all his cold and hard demeanor, he immediately softens when he sees his youngest sister, Lilias, and Sophie notices how protective he is of her. Lilias has an unreasonable fear of bones, so much so, that all knives and sharp tools must be hidden as she has a tendency to want to cut her bones out of her body. Rebecca? No one speaks of Rebecca. No one is allowed entry into her room, which is filled with a creepy collection of antique dolls that Rebecca used to love and play with. <br /><br />That first night, Sophie could hear voices coming out of Rebecca's room, and tries to investigate. She later finds out that Lilias can hear them too, and she knows who these voices belong to. The dolls. The dolls are speaking to her, luring her, but she tells Sophie she has to ignore them, she can't listen to the dolls because they tell her to do bad things. <br /><br />Ouija board, ghost of a little girl, creepy talking dolls, and an old house full of weirdos? Yep. You got yourself a recipe for disaster. One that will scare the living daylights out of you.<br /><br />As the events unfold, and things reach a climax, we start to figure out who's who, what's going on, who's orchestrating the whole thing, why is the ghost haunting Sophie, and who's going to die next? If I were Sophie, I would've left as soon as I realized things weren't normal at this household. Sophie is a stubborn one though, and she's somehow convinced that figuring out what's happening will help her figure out what happened to her best friend, Jay. <br /><br />The ending was written brilliantly, and had all the right elements to cause you fear and panic, as well as that rush of adrenaline you get when you know the whole gig is up. <br /><br />I recently found out that a prequel had been released, and I've immediately ordered it! Just the thing I need for this season, so I can't wait to receive it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14658332802971912336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
